• The black queen on g3 moves horizontally along rank 3 to d3 (path: g3 → f3 → e3 → d3). All intervening squares are empty.
• After Qd3 is played, white’s king on d1 is in check along the d–file.
• The white king’s escape squares are:
 – c1 (controlled by the black bishop on f4 via the diagonal f4–e3–d2–c1)
 – c2 (controlled by the queen on d3 diagonally)
 – d2 (covered by both queen and bishop)
 – e2 (attacked by the queen on d3)
 – e1 (covered by the rook on e8 along the e–file)
• With no way to block or capture the queen, this move is checkmate.

Based on the current board, one idea to seize the initiative as Black is to use the king actively. Notice that the white rook sitting on b6 is eyeing your pawn on b4. Instead of simply moving that pawn (which still risks its loss), you can try to “attack” the rook while centralizing your king. One candidate move is to move your black king from d7 to c7. (In UCI notation that’s d7c7.) From c7 your king will be adjacent to b6, forcing White to decide how to save the rook—and giving you time to catch up in activity.

If you’d like to see the list of legal moves before committing, just let me know; otherwise, you can complete your turn with:

make_move d7c7

Player_Black (to Proxy):

Based on the position, one attractive option is to use the queen to give an immediate check. In particular, moving your queen from d3 to b3 is quite forcing. Note that from d3 the queen can legally move to b3 along the horizontal, as the path via c3 is clear. Once on b3 the queen attacks up the b‐file, checking the white king on b4. Moreover, b3 is covered by the black pawn on a4 (since a pawn on a4 can capture on b3 when moving forward), so the white king cannot capture the queen.

Thus, I recommend:

make_move d3b3

That means black’s rook on d7 (found on the second rank, square d7) is in danger of being captured on white’s next move. One good way to save the rook is to block the queen’s diagonal by advancing the pawn from c7 to c6. This move (c7c6) covers the square c6, so the queen on b5 no longer sees d7 along that diagonal. So, as Black I will play:

Player_Black (to Proxy):

The previous move didn’t address the check. Notice that White’s bishop on h7 is directly checking our king on g8 (they’re adjacent on the h7–g8 diagonal). To get out of check, we must either capture the checking piece or move the king. None of our pieces can capture the bishop safely, so our only option is to move the king.

The only safe square for our king is h8. Therefore, I’ll play:

make_move g8h8
